Twenty-One Public Buses Burned Down in South Shanghai 134

Lead Plumber Causes Disaster While Repairing Car

Losses Exceed 60,000 Yuan

At around 2:00 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the parking lot of the Shanghai South Public Bus Company, located south of the Siming Guild Hall on Xinqiao Road in the South City, destroying a total of twenty-one buses, with losses exceeding 60,000 yuan. The details are recorded below:

Development of Public Bus Business: The Shanghai South Public Bus Company has been in operation for three years, and the routes have been expanded to four. The first route starts from Lao Ximen, passes through Guohuo Road, and circles to the Sixteenth Pier. The second route goes between Longhua and West Gate. The third route goes along Zhonghua Road. The fourth route starts from Xujiahui in West Shanghai and goes to the Hongqiao Road Airport. Recently, since April 1st, a special bus for Longhua has been added, and the business is growing daily, with the number of vehicles increasing to more than forty. There is still a situation where supply cannot meet demand.

Red-Hot Soldering Iron Accidentally Touches Gasoline: Unexpectedly, at around 2:00 AM yesterday morning, Zhuang Baogen, a lead plumber, was repairing the No. 8 bus in the parking lot of the company's parking lot south of the Siming Guild Hall on Xinqiao Road when he accidentally touched the red-hot soldering iron to the gasoline, suddenly starting a fire that quickly spread. At that time, it was late at night, and all the workers in the factory had returned home to sleep and could not rescue it.

Twenty-One Buses Burned: The fire was extremely fierce at the time. Fortunately, the fire brigades from various districts heard the alarm one after another and drove to rescue it. The fire lasted for an hour and thirty minutes before being extinguished at 3:30 AM. A total of five Qianyi Musi brand cars, two Dodge brand cars, two Ford brand cars, and twelve Chevrolet brand cars were destroyed. The company numbers were 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 12, 14, 17, 18, 21, 24, 26, 29, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, a total of twenty-one vehicles.

Photograph of Shanghai South Public Bus After the Fire (Taken by This Newspaper)

Both the Bus Factory and the Houses Were Insured: After the incident, Director Wang of the Second District sent an inspector to investigate the truth of the fire. Soon after, the factory director Ni Pihuan sent a letter to Director Wang, stating that the factory buildings were insured for 4,000 taels of silver and the 35 buses were insured for 52,500 taels of silver. The British Norwegian Qiyou Ning Insurance Company insured 7/12 and the Phoenix Insurance Company insured 5/12, it is said.

The Company Discusses Post-Disaster Issues: Zhuang Baogen, the lead plumber who caused the disaster, fled the scene at the time and was subsequently located. The factory director sent a letter to Director Wang with Zhuang and Zhang A'si (32 years old, from Taizhou), the worker on duty, both of whom were sent to the Second District. After Director Wang's detailed questioning, except for Zhang A'si, who was temporarily released on bail by the factory, Zhuang Baogen, the lead plumber, was temporarily detained in the district, waiting to be sent to the General Bureau for handling. The company then convened an emergency meeting of the directors and supervisors yesterday afternoon, deciding to reorganize the remaining vehicles to maintain traffic on the second and third routes and to quickly find ways to restore the original state of the first and fourth routes, it is said.

Attempted Kidnapping of Zhu Ligeng Fails 135

Cabby Cleverly Presses Alarm Bell to Report Arrest

Bodyguard Courageously Opens Fire on Bandits

Zhu Ligeng, a local who runs the Zhongfu Silk Factory at No. 28 Jinling Road in Zhabei, lives at No. 215 Changsha Road in the Public Concession. He owns a car, registration number 10320. Because he has been receiving threatening letters demanding large sums of money, Zhu hired a bodyguard named Wang Xuesheng, who carried a handgun, for safety and to accompany him in and out to prepare for any eventuality. At around 8:30 AM yesterday morning, Zhu intended to go to the factory in Zhabei to take care of matters and ordered the driver Chen Xiangyun, assistant Wang A'san, and the bodyguard to be ready. Just as Zhu Ligeng was about to step into the car, four kidnappers suddenly stepped forward. Three of the kidnappers held handguns, forcing the driver and others to get out of the car. They ordered Zhu to get into the car. Fortunately, the driver Chen Xiangyun was quite clever. After getting out of the car, he immediately ran back into the room and pressed the alarm bell, reporting to the Xinza police station. At this time, the bodyguard Wang Xuesheng also displayed great courage. In order to preemptively strike, he drew his handgun and opened fire on the bandits, firing five bullets, none of which hit. However, the kidnappers did not dare to take action at this point and had to abandon their attempt to kidnap the wealthy and flee for their lives. Soon after, armed Chinese and foreign detectives from the Xinza police station rushed to the scene and surrounded and searched the area. However, the bandits had already fled far away and could not be traced. They had no choice but to search the surrounding area and arrest two suspects, taking them to the police station for interrogation.

Dog Racing is Banned 136

Police Station Dispatches Police to Prohibit Vehicle Traffic

Ming Garden Only Held One Race Last Night Before Ceasing

The Shanghai Public Concession Board has decided to prohibit dog racing gambling in the concession from the 1st of this month. Yesterday was the dog racing period at Ming Garden. In order to implement the ban, the Huishan police station first dispatched Chinese and foreign armed police officers to block all roads leading to Ming Garden from 7:00 PM last night, prohibiting vehicles from traveling. Pedestrians were allowed to pass on foot. Sixty Chinese and foreign police officers were dispatched to station at each entrance of Ming Garden, allowing people to exit but not to enter. In addition, there were two large red police vehicles full of police officers parked nearby to prevent accidents. However, the lights at the Ming Garden dog racing track were still brightly lit as usual. About forty members had already entered the venue early. At 8:30 PM, they actually held one dog race before ceasing. This can be said to be the last burst of light from the end of the world for dog racing. Before long, the dog racing staff and members in the venue left one after another, chatting and laughing nonchalantly. The police did not interfere. A Western woman holding fresh flowers joked with a Western police officer, saying that she lost 40 yuan in the one race. At that time, most of the lights in the venue were also turned off one after another. At 9:15 PM, the roads were reopened to traffic. Seeing that there was no activity at the dog racing track, the Western police chief ordered the Chinese and foreign police officers at the entrance of Ming Garden to march away in formation. As for Shen Garden, there was no activity at all last night.

Order to Close Temples Set Up in Rented Houses 137

Instructions from the Municipal Public Security Bureau

Instructions from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau: In order to comply with the order, it has been found that temples set up in rented houses in this city were originally limited to the end of 1930 and must be ordered to close down. Subsequently, Municipal Government Instruction No. 6805 was received, stating that the request from the Chinese Buddhist Association to postpone the ban should be approved and ordered to be reviewed and reported by this bureau. It was then proposed to extend the deadline by three months to the end of March this year. Subsequently, Municipal Government Instruction No. 8632 was received and approved, and an order was issued for compliance. Now that the deadline has expired, the ban should be implemented. However, it is feared that the abbots of these temples may use excuses to delay or resist compliance. If they do not comply, they will be executed on their behalf in accordance with the Administrative Execution Law. All idols and Bodhisattvas can be sent to nearby temples, and a report on the compliance should be submitted. This order is issued on April of the Republic of China. [signed] Chen Xizeng, Director of the Bureau.

The Two Bandits in Serial Murder Cases Executed by Firing Squad Yesterday 138

The notorious bandits, Zhang Amao and Gui Jinhua, both from Ningbo, repeatedly opened fire in the Public Concession between May and October of the 17th year [of the Republic, i.e. 1928], killing people. For example, Yu Shunxiang was killed in Chengji Lane on North Zhejiang Road, Wu Pengfei was killed in Ruikang Lane on East Jiaxing Road, and Wang Chengcai was killed on Zhaofeng Road. When Western Constable Bai Laosi saw this and tried to arrest them, he was also shot and killed. They also shot and killed the English woman, Thomson, on Route des Soeurs. The sentence was reported to the provincial government, and approval for execution by hanging was received. Yesterday morning, the Special District Court ordered the police station to bring the two convicts, Zhang and Gui, from the Western Prison. Judge Cheng questioned them about any last words. Both convicts said that since their death was imminent, notifying their families would only increase their sorrow, so they had nothing else to say, only requesting wine and food. Judge Cheng then ordered a court clerk to purchase food. After they finished eating, they were escorted onto a prison van and sent to the Jiangsu Second Prison execution ground in Caohejing. A letter was sent to the Shanghai Local Court requesting them to send an executioner and a supervising prosecutor to the scene. Zhang and Gui were brought forward again, their identities were verified, and then the executioner tied them up and hanged them according to the law. The gallows were sealed, and the bodies were left exposed overnight as usual. After re-examination this morning, the bodies were claimed by relatives for burial.

Currently a Member of the Zhabei Defense Corps

Ma Yuankai, a native of Chuansha and an employee of the Shenchang Foreign Firm at No. 622 Xipuyi Lane, Qipu Road, South Area of the Special District Court, was robbed of cash, clothes, and jewelry on the 1st of this month, as reported in the previous newspaper. It has now been learned that the robbery was initiated by Wang Agen, a relative of Ma. Wang lives at No. 124 Song Park Road, Zhabei, and is currently a member of the Zhabei Defense Corps. At the time, Wang colluded with Yan Lingxiang, a local, Wang Nanrong, from Shaonan, and Xiao Guisheng, and others, and went to Ma's house to rob him. After the robbery, an internal conflict arose due to the uneven distribution of the loot. Yan turned himself in to the General Police Station the day before yesterday. He confessed that he had received a raccoon fur coat, which he had already pawned. He presented the pawn ticket. He also stated that Xiao lived at No. 11 Huaanfang, Huaxing Road, Zhabei, and that Wang Nanrong was playing in the China Park on Sichuan Road. The head constable immediately sent Detective Xie Shuiquan and Detective Zhao Zifang to the park first and arrested Wang Nanrong. Then they went to Zhabei, and together with the police detectives, they arrested Wang and Xiao. Yesterday morning, the police bureau of the area brought the two robbers to the Special District Local Court. Judge Zhou interrogated them. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu briefly described the case and requested that a document be sent to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to transfer the two robbers to custody for further investigation. Western Detective Mei Sheng presented a blade and a pistol that the robbers had abandoned at the victim's home while fleeing. However, the pistol was a fake. Ma's maid, Lu, was brought to the court and identified the defendants as the robbers who were at the scene. When questioned, the two robbers admitted the robbery without hesitation, but claimed that all the loot they had received had been lost in gambling dens that day. Judge Zhou then ordered the defendants to be taken back into custody and adjourned the hearing for fourteen days.

Accusation of Incest by Uncle Against Nephew for Adultery with Aunt 141

Resulting in Insufficient Evidence for a Guilty Verdict

Li Shangcun, a native of Suqian, 51 years old, and his wife, Li Zhang, run a beef shop at No. 202 Xinzha Bridge together. Li Daxin, a cousin's son, also works in the shop. Recently, Li Shangcun accused his nephew in the Special District Court of raping his aunt and requested legal action. Yesterday, Judge Ge opened the court for trial. According to Li Shangcun, he used to be a small patrolman for the Fourth Road Police Station. In November of the 18th year of the Republic [i.e. 1929], he suffered from hemiplegia due to a cold on night duty and retired. He opened a beef shop. On January 15th of this year, his illness worsened, and he was unable to get out of bed. On the night of the 18th, his wife, Zhang, was threatened by his nephew with a fake pistol, thrown to the floor, and forcibly raped. Later, in the morning, he used the same means to threaten Zhang to leave home and live at No. 14 next to the Chenjiabang small vegetable market. On the morning of January 24th, Li Mingshan, a mailman No. 123 at the Caojiadu Post Office, accompanied her to her brother's house in Shaoxing, where she stayed for fifteen days. Later, Li Shangcun received the news and went back with her. Li Daxin claimed to be 36 years old and said that the accusation of raping his aunt was completely false. He said that when the plaintiff opened the beef shop, he invested 200 yuan. Recently, the shop was sold last December for 380 yuan. Because of the capital relationship, he asked his uncle for the money and even asked his cousin, Li Mingshan, to intercede. Unexpectedly, the plaintiff intended to deny the debt and falsely accused him of rape to embezzle the money. Li Mingshan also stated that the debt collection had failed and that the matter of accompanying Li Zhang back to Shaoxing was completely fabricated. Judge Ge questioned the plaintiff repeatedly and pronounced the sentence that day, ruling that there was insufficient evidence and declaring the defendant not guilty.

Yesterday's Windstorm on the Huangpu River Causes Damage 142

Yesterday afternoon, the south wind picked up considerably, and after 5:00 PM, the wind intensified. Dust and sand flew wildly on the streets, and many shop signs along the Huangpu River were blown off by the strong wind. Pedestrians were also hindered by the dust and sand. Cargo ships heavily laden in the Huangpu River were overturned by the strong winds and waves. One such ship was the Meng Tingsheng, which was carrying 200 barrels of tung oil and foreign and domestic goods to Huzhou for delivery. In the afternoon, it was moored at the south end of the Dalai Wharf in Pudong, waiting for the tide to set sail. Unexpectedly, at about 6:00 PM, when the wind was at its strongest, it capsized due to the heavy load and the strong waves. The crew members also fell into the water. Except for those who were rescued, the whereabouts of one crew member are unknown, and the losses are substantial. The consignees have hired ships to salvage the sunken ship and cargo. Another rice boat, the Wang Guangyu, from the interior, fully loaded with rice and stone, came to Shanghai to be sold by the rice merchant Wang. Yesterday afternoon, when it was sailing on the Longhua section of the South Huangpu River, it was hit by wind and waves, and all the rice in the boat was soaked with water. Two crew members were swept away by the wind. Wang, seeing this, immediately steered the rudder straight towards the shore and anchored, so it did not face danger. However, the loss was already considerable. Wang reported and prepared to hire a ship to transport the wet rice to Shanghai to be sold to sugar mills. The Chengfengyu Company's barge, Shen Asan, carrying sandalwood firewood, also lost a lot of cargo in the Rihui Port due to the wind and waves, and the oars and equipment on the ship were also blown off, but fortunately, the ship was unharmed. It is reported that the cargo is insured. Zhao Er'er, a wharf boatman, transported wheat and miscellaneous grains from Fengjing and other places to Shanghai. When it sailed near Longhua Mouth, it was suddenly hit by a hurricane and giant waves. Unable to withstand it, the ship tilted to one side, causing most of the wheat to spill into the Huangpu River. Fortunately, the whole ship did not capsize, and it quickly sailed to the shore to take temporary shelter. In addition, many instruments were washed away by the wind and waves. Therefore, the cargo ships moored in the Huangpu River hired ships to unload the cargo to lighten the load and avoid danger.

Publication of the Public Concession's Budget Proposal for This Year 143

Includes Recent Resident Opposition to the

Estimated Rental Assessment and Collection of Police Tax

The Public Concession's budget proposal for this year was published yesterday and will be submitted to the annual meeting of foreign taxpayers on the 15th of this month for approval. The total amount of regular income for this year, including the surplus of silver 2,271,570 taels from the previous year's regular budget proposal, is estimated to be 16,939,870 taels of silver. The estimated regular expenditure is 16,626,800 taels of silver. Subtracting the two, there is still a surplus of silver 313,070 taels, which will be transferred to the regular income and expenditure items for 1932. The total amount of special income for this year is estimated to be 17,992,500 taels of silver. This number includes 14,134,800 taels of silver from the sale of the electricity department in installments, 250,000 taels of silver from the sale of surplus land, some miscellaneous income, and 3,344,700 taels of silver from the previous year's surplus. The estimated special expenditure, including the repayment of municipal bonds of 8,125,900 taels of silver, is 18,342,250 taels of silver. Subtracting the two, there is a shortfall of 350,750 taels of silver, which will be transferred to the special income and expenditure items for 1932 to offset the shortfall.

Regular income: Land tax of 3,900,000 taels of silver, an increase of 1,147,500 taels of silver compared to last year's estimate, due to the re-evaluation of land prices. The land tax is still collected at a rate of 7/1000 for the second half of last year. The income from the tax is 5,800,000 taels of silver, an increase of 310,000 taels of silver compared to last year's estimate, still collected at the rate of 14% for the second half of last year. Special police tax income is 325,000 taels of silver, an increase of 75,000 taels of silver compared to last year's estimate, still collected at the rate of 12% for the second half of last year. Special advertising tax is 20,000 taels of silver, the same as the amount listed in last year's budget proposal. Wharfage dues are 750,000 taels of silver, an increase of 75,000 taels of silver compared to last year's estimate. License fees are 1,829,950 taels of silver, an increase of 90,650 taels of silver, including 50,000 taels of silver increased from the license fees for public bus lines, automobiles, and freight vehicles. The total amount of these items is estimated to be 820,000 taels of silver, compared to 579,000 taels of silver last year. In addition, the tax on privately owned rickshaws can increase by 27,000 taels of silver, the tax on food vendors can increase by 5,000 taels of silver, the tax on foreign theaters can increase by 7,000 taels of silver, the tax on bicycles can increase by 7,000 taels of silver, and the tax on temporary liquor permits for hotels and foreign wine shops can increase by 4,000 taels of silver. The tax on Chinese hotels can increase by 3,000 taels of silver. The estimated rental income from municipal properties is 29,500 taels of silver, an increase of 59,000 taels of silver compared to last year, due to the opening of the Fuzhou Road vegetable market. The estimated income from public and municipal enterprises is 1,256,350 taels of silver, an increase of 102,790 taels of silver compared to last year, because the gold pound dividends that the municipal council receives from Shanghai Waterworks should increase by 68,450 taels of silver due to the high price of gold and the low price of silver. In addition, the Shanghai Power Company should pay the municipal council 5% of its total income for the electricity sold. This item is estimated to be 706,000 taels of silver, an increase of 36,000 taels of silver compared to last year. The fees paid by public buses and French tram companies for passing through the roads in the Public Concession are the same as last year. The bonus paid by the Shanghai Tram Company will be slightly reduced compared to last year. The fees paid by the company's trolleybuses for passing through various roads are the same as last year. The municipal brick and tile factory is expected to increase its surplus by 15,000 taels of silver. The income from prison labor and the surplus from the Pingqiao stone mine and the engineering office factory are the same as last year. In addition, the municipal council's shares in the China and Foreign Telephone Company were repurchased by the company last year, so there is no income to speak of. In addition, miscellaneous income is listed as 492,000 taels of silver, an increase of 412,000 taels of silver compared to last year. In addition, the surplus of 2,271,570 taels of silver from regular expenses in 1930 is also included in this year's income item. As for the taxes collected, the municipal council plans to collect 7/1000 of the newly assessed land price for land tax within the concession, to be paid in advance in the first and second half of the year. The police tax is planned to be collected from April 1, 1931, until the next meeting of foreign taxpayers, and for buildings within the concession, it will be changed to 14% of the estimated rental assessment, to be paid in advance on a quarterly basis. The special tax collected from buildings outside the concession according to the water, electricity, and telephone contracts will also be changed to 12% of the estimated rental assessment from April 1, 1931. In addition, the special advertising tax will be increased from 1 qian of silver per square foot per year to 3 qian of silver per square foot per year, according to Announcement No. 444, to be paid at the time of license application.

Regular expenditure: The expenses of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps are listed as 212,170 taels of silver, an increase of 57,000 taels of silver compared to last year. The expenses of the Russian Volunteer Corps are listed as 228,680 taels of silver, an increase of 58,560 taels of silver compared to last year. The expenses of the Fire Department are listed as 693,630 taels of silver, an increase of 110,630 taels of silver compared to last year. The expenses of the Police Department are listed as 6,708,790 taels of silver, including the three groups of patrol, prison, and legal affairs, an increase of 1,308,060 taels of silver compared to last year. The increase in expenses is mostly due to increased salaries, the shortening of the exchange rate of the sterling, and some expansion of several police teams. In addition, there is a newly proposed plan to eliminate bandits, which also requires expenses of 112,540 taels of silver. The expenses of the Health Department are 1,075,570 taels of silver, an increase of 227,530 taels of silver compared to last year. The various subsidies and grants are listed as 180,130 taels of silver, an increase of 46,730 taels of silver compared to last year. The expenses of the Engineering Department are 4,438,790 taels of silver, an increase of 682,870 taels of silver compared to last year. The expenses of the Music Corps are 182,930 taels of silver, an increase of 36,120 taels of silver. The expenses of the Public Library are 8,020 taels of silver, an increase of 820 taels of silver. The expenses of the Education Department, including school supplies, are 1,150,440 taels of silver, an increase of 470,190 taels of silver compared to last year. In addition, the expenses of the Accounting Department, the General Office, the Secretary-General's Office, and the Chinese Research and Translation Office have all increased compared to last year.

Special expenditure: Under the special expenditure items, there are bridges of 110,000 taels of silver, ditches of 91,700 taels of silver, sewers of 352,000 taels of silver, wharves of 299,500 taels of silver, land acquisition of 593,800 taels of silver, houses of 6,167,970 taels of silver, roads of 2,300,000 taels of silver, and other buildings of 30,000 taels of silver.

Statement from the Standing Committee of the Anti-Opium Association Regarding the Bai Case 144

Believes It Is Entirely False Accusation

Huang Jiawei, the director-general of the Chinese National Anti-Opium Association, accompanied his wife, Ms. Bai Zhiying, to Taiwan to inspect the opium prohibition situation. During their absence from Shanghai, various Chinese and foreign newspapers suddenly reported that Ms. Bai Zhiying, Huang's wife, was found by Hong Kong Customs to be privately trafficking in morphine. Mr. and Mrs. Huang returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday. It is understood that after this case occurred, the association held an emergency meeting of the Standing Committee and resolved to telegraph Director-General Huang to return to Shanghai immediately to clarify the truth. Now that Mr. and Mrs. Huang have returned, a special meeting was held yesterday, attended by Wang Jingqi, Li Denghui, Guo Baoyi, Shen Gao, and lawyer Cai Rudong, among other committee members. (1) First, Huang Jiawei reported on the trip to Taiwan. (2) Huang Jiawei reported on the truth of the false accusation. (3) Examined various evidence of false accusation. (4) The standing committee members considered that Mr. Huang's reasons for the false accusation and the evidence against it were sufficient and immediately resolved to issue the following statement on the Bai case. As reported earlier, the rumors of Ms. Bai Zhiying's trafficking in morphine, because Ms. Bai is the wife of Huang Jiawei, director-general of this association, have a special relationship with this association, so we paid close attention. At that time, because Mr. and Mrs. Huang were on official business in Taiwan, the rumors came suddenly, and without knowing the truth, it was not appropriate to express any opinion. We telegraphed Mr. Huang to return to Shanghai early to clarify the truth. Now that Mr. Huang and his wife have returned to Shanghai and reported everything to the special meeting of the Standing Committee of this association, and submitted many pieces of evidence, after detailed inquiries and various studies by the committee members of this association, we believe that the rumors of Ms. Bai's incident are groundless and hereby declare this. (5) Resolved to ask Director-General Huang to resume his duties immediately.

Money Dealers Demand Separate Regulations for Native Banks 145

Local Support

Since the Legislative Yuan passed the Banking Law No. 1, which subsumed native banks under it, the Native Banks Association has held meetings to discuss it, unanimously stating that banks and native banks are fundamentally different. The most obvious is that banks are limited organizations, while native banks are joint ventures with unlimited liability. Furthermore, there are differences in business, nature, and customs, and they have a long history. General commercial capital relies on native banks for loans to regulate it. If the native bank law is not enacted separately but is subsumed under the Banking Law, it will affect the entire commercial sector, and the consequences are unimaginable. Therefore, we have already submitted reports to various government agencies, requesting separate regulations for native banks to be followed, and sent letters to colleagues in various ports to jointly support our cause in order to achieve our goal. Details were recorded in the previous newspaper. It is now reported that various ports have responded, and the incoming letters are recorded below: (1) Letter from the Nanjing Native Banks Association: Respectfully, we received your letter and a draft submission. Our association believes that native banks and banks cannot be mentioned in the same breath. The Banking Law passed by the Legislative Yuan forcibly subsumes native banks under banks. All kinds of obstacles and difficulties are as stated in your letter. Investigating native banks and banks, there are many differences in their nature and customs. Native banks are operated by partners, while banks are limited organizations. The procedures for deposits and withdrawals are different. Furthermore, native banks have a long history and are widely established in towns and villages. The customs that have been followed are difficult to change at once. If we suddenly follow the banking regulations, it will inevitably affect the entire industry. Therefore, it is necessary to collect the opinions of the national financial community and properly formulate the native bank law to distinguish it from banks, so that it can be implemented and followed. Our association held a meeting and resolved to unanimously support your association's proposal and requested your association to strive hard to ensure that the native bank law is drafted as soon as possible for the public good. (2) Letter from the Kaifeng Native Banks Association in Henan: Respectfully, we received your letter and a draft submission. We respectfully acknowledge your association's enthusiasm for public welfare and the utmost intention to maintain the native banking industry. We should proceed together to achieve our goal. In addition to sending separate telegrams and making unanimous requests, we are enclosing a copy of the telegram draft for your review. (Enclosed telegram text: "To the Central Political Conference of the Chinese Kuomintang, the National Government, the Legislative Yuan, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry, we have read the submission from the Shanghai Native Banks Association, stating that the regulations for native banks are important and that subsuming them under other laws would be difficult. We urge you to separately draft regulations for native banks to avoid being subsumed under the Banking Law to be followed. After the native banks read it, we express our agreement and unanimously urge your committee (government) (yuan) (departments) to review, approve the separate drafting of regulations for native banks, facilitate the implementation, and avoid difficulties, for the public good." etc.) In addition, there are also the Native Banks Associations of Hangzhou City, and the Native Banks Associations of "Changshu," "Pinghu," and "Nantong," among other counties, which have sent letters in response, calling for concerted efforts to strive to achieve the goal. The original texts and the above-mentioned intentions are mostly different in wording but the same in meaning, and are not recorded in detail.

The pirates also returned fire. After about an hour, the bandits were defeated and fled. At present, the Changjiang ship is still being salvaged. Petition from the National Goods Maintenance Association to Prevent Foreigners from Establishing Factories 149

The Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association submitted a document to the National Government, stating: "We have observed that since our country was forced under the walls of a city and the opening of the sea borders, various countries have wielded the unparalleled weapon of unequal treaties, exerting their utmost to implement economic aggression policies. They drain the marrow and blood of our people to cultivate their influence in China. In those times, those in power were unworthy, holding power upside down. All authorities only knew to consolidate favor and pursue personal gain, neglecting to intervene. This led to a continuous influx of foreign goods, increasing year after year. All kinds of items needed by our nation for clothing, food, housing, transportation, and daily use were usurped from domestic production and replaced by foreign goods. Eventually, our wealth was exhausted, the country weakened, and we fell into a semi-colonial status without realizing it, a truly lamentable situation. Fearing the peril of the nation and lamenting the demise of domestic products, our association gathered various industries, businesses, factories, and patriotic comrades in the year of Xinhai (one year before the founding of the Republic of China) to initiate and organize, with the aim of awakening the public, maintaining national goods, promoting industry, and expanding foreign sales. We also strived to advocate for the abolition of unequal treaties, the recovery of tariff autonomy, the recovery of extraterritorial rights, and the abolition of consular jurisdiction, among other major纲领, to save the nation. Since the unification of our National Government, adhering to the late Premier's instructions and after much arduous work, we have been able to gradually implement the above-mentioned matters and are approaching our goals. This is truly a good opportunity for our country to revive. However, at a time when gold is expensive and silver is cheap, and a狂潮 sweeps high, industrialists from various countries, seeing that our country has tariff autonomy and increased import taxes, have suddenly changed their tactics of economic aggression. Wielding their abundant capital, they are flocking to China to establish factories, using cheap Chinese labor and skilled techniques, hoping to avoid our country's increased tariffs and maximize the production of their goods, a vicious plan to夺國貨 and eliminate sales channels for national goods. Recently, the number of factories established in China by countries such as Britain and Japan has been increasing day by day and month by month. This is evidenced by the facts reported on March 22nd and 31st of this year, which already give a general idea of their intensified aggression. Given the current decline of domestic industry and commerce in our country, the消沉 of all industries, and the奄奄一息 of national goods, how can we resist this powerful enemy of new economic aggression? We, in our ignorance, believe that under these circumstances, our National Government should urgently establish special regulations for the registration and licensing of foreign factories in China, strictly restricting their establishment and levying重税 upon them. After approval, they should be constantly監　, preventing their aggressive actions to avoid倾轧 with our national goods, thereby rescuing the幼年期 of national goods. Our association, aware of this and feeling危, hereby submits this special电陈述貢獻蒭蕘, humbly requesting that the钧府院部 carefully examine and approve it, swiftly implement it, and await orders with utmost anxiety. We also respectfully request instructions for our compliance. Respectfully, Wang Jie'an, Wang Xingyi, and Wang Hanqiang, Standing Committee Members of the Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association,叩首."

Important News from the Maritime Industry 154

The Headquarters Sends Troops to Escort Ships: Following the incidents of gambling bandits causing disturbances and injuring crew members on ships such as the Changjiang ships Jiang'an and Jiangshun, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company twice requested the Headquarters to send troops to protect the ships. The first request was rejected by the Capital Garrison Headquarters. Subsequently, General Manager Li submitted a request to Chairman Jiang for approval. Yesterday, the Headquarters approved the request, ordering the Capital Garrison Headquarters to dispatch five to four special service soldiers to each Yangtze River ship to provide escort. The first batch of nine fully armed soldiers has already been dispatched, with five stationed on the Jiangshun and four stationed on the Jianguo. The Bureau has been ordered to contact the Garrison Headquarters to dispatch troops for the remaining seven ships.

Sailors and workers in Shantou have implemented a boycott of French ships. Furthermore, British ships sailing between Shanghai and Shantou recently raised passenger fares due to the rising price of gold. Various circles in Shantou requested an exemption from the increase, but the shipping company did not agree. Passenger associations have proposed unanimously ceasing to travel on British ships and stopping loading their cargo.

The Old Pavilion in Gelao Lane Was Demolished Yesterday 156

There was a stone memorial archway called the "Gelao (Grand Secretary) Pavilion" of Xu Wendinggong, a Ming Dynasty grand secretary, located at the northern end of the County Bridge on Zhaojiabang Road in Shanghai City. Since its construction, it had stood for over three hundred years. Recently, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, considering that the archway obstructed road administration, planned to demolish it. Despite repeated petitions from the descendants of the Xu family to preserve it, the Bureau ordered workers to demolish it yesterday.

Recently, the weather has been abnormal, and smallpox is prevalent. The Chinese Red Cross has decided to send several doctors and nurses, as well as ambulances, to the concessions and inland areas starting from the 1st of this month to administer smallpox vaccinations and injections for disease prevention.

Zeng Youquan Will Be Buried in the Wannian Cemetery 160

Zeng Youquan, platoon leader of the fifth team of the Shanghai South District Defense Corps, died on September 1, 1928, in Longhua Road while chasing robbers, after being shot and seriously wounded by bandits. The coffin was temporarily placed in the QuanZhang Villa and has not yet been buried. After the team leader, Zeng Zemin, reported to his superiors and received approval, the deceased platoon leader was promoted to the rank of captain. It was also decided that the coffin would be buried in the Wannian Cemetery on April 12. The head and deputy heads, Ye Huijun and Wang Zhuangfei, found that the deceased captain Zeng Youquan had served the local area and sacrificed himself. His性可憐 and his志可嘉. The Verdict in the Case of the Tragic Death of Patrolman Li Qingfu's Eldest Daughter-in-Law 164

Li and His Three Sons Are Not Guilty

His Wife Died of Illness in Prison

Li Zhang, the eldest daughter-in-law of Li Qingfu, a patrolman from Anhui Province with number 615 at the Third Head of the Gordon Road Patrol Station, died by hanging herself at home at 666 Gordon Road on the night of August 27th last year. The patrol station, based on a letter from someone stating that the deceased had been strangled to death by her parents-in-law and husband, detained Li, his wife Chen, his eldest son Li Yulong, and his second son Li Yukun and handed them over to the Special District Local Court for interrogation and detention. Li Chen died of illness in the women's prison. Presiding Judge Wu repeatedly interrogated Li Qingfu and his three sons, but they all denied murder. In order to clarify the truth, Judge Wu personally went to the deceased's room to investigate. Recently, the辩論 ended, and the verdict was announced yesterday morning: Li Qingfu and his three sons are all not guilty. They had been detained for more than half a year and have now been released, which is a great stroke of luck within misfortune.

An Old Woman Files a Case of "Robbing a Bride" 165

The Defendant Claims It Was a Wedding

Zhang Li, a woman from Nanhui, is 60 years old. She recently sued Zhu Alin, Zhu Akun, Zhu Asan, Chen Caigen, and others at the Special District Court for the crime of "robbing a bride" and obstructing freedom. Her statement of claim stated that her daughter, Zhang Xuezhen, was forcibly abducted by the defendants at the age of 19 to cohabit with Zhu Akun. Two months later, she took advantage of an opportunity to return home. This happened eight years ago. Since then, her reputation has been ruined, and she has not yet been married. In May of last year, Chen Caigen and others abducted her daughter again and imprisoned her privately. She earnestly requested legal action, etc. Yesterday, Judge Ge Zhitan opened the trial. Zhang Li供如上述. Zhu Asan stated that he lived at 384 Xintangjia Lane. Zhu Akun had a hearing impairment and was represented by him. He said that Zhang Xuezhen was currently in Nanhui and was very peaceful. When Xuezhen was five years old, she was already a 童养媳 in the Zhu family. At the age of twelve, she returned to her mother's home. At the age of nineteen, she was welcomed and married, and there were媒帖 as evidence. They cohabited for four years and had two daughters, both of whom died young. Last May, someone was sent to bring her back. Zhang Li's accusation of "robbing" etc. had no factual basis and was for other purposes, etc. Since Zhang Xuezhen had not arrived, the case was adjourned for further investigation and interrogation.

A Male Corpse with a Decomposed Face 170

Yesterday morning at about 8 o'clock, a patrol boat from the Wusong Lifesaving Bureau recovered an unidentified male corpse in the Huangpu River near the Guanghua Oil Pond in Wusong. He was about 30 years old, with no injuries. It was unclear whether he had fallen in by accident or committed suicide. However, his face was already rotten, suggesting he had been in the water for a long time. The corpse was wearing a white Western-style shirt, blue lined jacket and pants, white belt, wool socks, and rubber overshoes. There was a Zhongshan watch and a leather wallet in his pocket, containing only 18 copper coins. There were no other possessions. He was immediately brought back to Wusong and reported to the Lifesaving Bureau. The details of the corpse were recorded, and after being photographed, a coffin was prepared by the charity organization for burial in the public cemetery, pending family recognition.

Free Talk

A Word of Insight 177

— Chi Fo

▲ The personality of a person is like the weather: lively and beautiful. Sanguine people are like spring: vigorous and passionate. Choleric people are like summer: desolate and bleak. Melancholic people are like autumn: restrained and cold. Phlegmatic people are like winter: rigid and cold. Heaven cannot be without the four seasons, and people cannot be without personality. Each of the four seasons has its own joy, and each personality has its own strengths.

▲ In angry rain and violent wind, birds are grieved. In bright breeze and clear sunshine, plants are delighted. It can be seen that heaven and earth cannot be without harmony for a day, and the human heart cannot be without joy for a day.

▲ Watching flowers half-bloomed and drinking wine slightly tipsy, there is great pleasure in this. If one reaches unrestrained drunkenness, it becomes an evil realm.

▲ Do not envy the wealth and honor of others; enjoy your own poverty and lowliness. Wealth and honor bring烦恼, while poverty and lowliness bring leisure. The true meaning of life lies here, not there.

▲ Vanity is the tomb of people, and children are the restraints of cattle and horses.

▲ Tobacco is named the "grass of longing." One cannot describe its taste but cannot help but long for it. Love can be called the "flower of anesthesia." One cannot describe its reason but cannot help but be anesthetized by it.

▲ Superstition is the element of success. Heroes become heroes, beauties become beauties, the wealthy become wealthy, and scholars become scholars all because of superstition. Therefore, there is a world because there is superstition; there is humanity because there is superstition; there is joy because there is superstition. If, one day, life is thoroughly understood and superstition is overthrown, then the end of the Earth will have arrived.

▲ The face is the public ledger of life; forehead wrinkles are like the final results that have already been announced. Alas, the people of the world are dreaming and do not know that old age is approaching.

Lihu Garden and Huishan Mountain Excursion Diary 178

— Fenlü

After visiting Plum Garden, a guest praised the beauty of Lihu Garden, so I went there very early on the fifteenth day to visit. The garden is located in Yangming Township, about fifteen or sixteen *li* from Wuxi city. I took a car instead of walking, and along the way saw mulberry trees and hemp fields. When I arrived at the gate, the morning dew had not yet dried. Light shade covered the willows by the *an*. Ancient trees surrounded broken pavilions, the scenery desolate. I exchanged a small amount of money for a ticket and entered. The garden occupies a corner of Tai Lake. A long corridor overlooks the water, and one can scoop up lake water by leaning over the railing. Inscriptions by Mi Xiangyang are embedded in the walls. I followed them and read until I forgot the distance. Passing a rockery, there was a patch of grass and three sailboats. Facing the lake is Jingxuan Tower. From there, one can watch light boats on the lake, entering and exiting the painted railings and willows, inspiring a broad and distant feeling in one’s heart that is not easily forgotten. Next to Jingxuan Tower is Lakeside Thatched Cottage, with exquisite bamboo blinds and a well-arranged layout. The plaque on the cottage was written by Qiu Changnian, his brushstrokes elegant and lively, perfectly matching the cottage. As for the name “Thatched Cottage,” there is Jiangshang Thatched Cottage in Bansong Garden in Shanghai, Jianshang Thatched Cottage in Suzhou, and Chishang Thatched Cottage in Wuxi Park. But in terms of occupying a secluded spot with undulating misty waters, Lakeside Cottage is the most outstanding. Turning west, one passes Little Peach Blossom Spring. The rock cave is deep and secluded. At first, one might think there was a hidden paradise. But the area draws water to form a pond and construct small pavilions, quickly revealing everything at a glance. The most wonderful thing is a lotus leaf made of cement in the center of the water, roughly the size of a round table. People can walk underneath it, truly creating the image of fish frolicking east of the lotus leaf and fish frolicking west of the lotus leaf. The surrounding rocks are inscribed with "Tiantian Island," a name that is exceptionally elegant and refined. As there were many visitors, I left. A few *wu* away from Lihu Garden is Lake Manor, where stones are being cut and clouds are being shaped, still awaiting completion. Earlier, Lü Ping, feeling tired, did not go to Lihu Garden and arranged to meet me later at the foot of Huiquan Mountain. When I arrived at Huishan Mountain, Ping had not yet arrived. I walked alone past “Separated from the Red Dust” and up to “Cloud Rising Pavilion,” gazing at the broken willows and grassy monument in Jichang Garden, as well as the Hometown Gentleman Shrine at the foot of the mountain, standing there in melancholy for a long time. On this excursion, although the landscape was beautiful, I couldn't escape my troubles. I remembered coming here last year when my old mother was still alive. Now, I climb Head Mao Peak alone, embracing the vast white clouds, thinking about where I belong and longing for the joy of someone pulling at my clothes and leaning against the door, never to be regained. I felt sorrow like the sea, and the misty waters of the Five Lakes were not enough to describe its depth. Before long, the mountains were darkening, and the desolate temple was shrouded in smoke. Lü Ping arrived, and we brewed tea together under Yilan Hall, tasting the second spring in the world, which left a lingering, sweet aftertaste like olives. Perhaps this trip was not in vain for Ping, who was burdened with worldly cares.

A Tale of a Loyal Dog Defending Against Thieves 179

— Zuichi Sheng

Some days ago, I went to a friend's house in Pudong for business and met a villager named Jia, who was talking eloquently about his beloved dog that died defending against thieves. I was moved by the dog's death, its dedication, and its fulfillment of its duty. Thus, I happily recorded the event. Jia lives in Zhangjialou. His family keeps several hunting dogs, all of whom are tame and understand human intentions. When they eat, they maintain order, each going to its own bowl and not interfering with others. Many village families raise chickens, often dozens. At night, chickens are often snatched and eaten by yellow wolves. Since Jia had his dogs on guard, he killed several wolves, and the wolves disappeared and dared not come out. One night, a thief climbed over the bamboo fence in the backyard, hoping to find something to steal. He was noticed by a dog named A Long, who barked madly at him and bit his foot. The thief, fearing he couldn't resist, jumped into a pond in the garden to avoid him. But the dog still didn't give up and also jumped in, fighting the thief to the death. The thief then took out a knife and stabbed the dog in the belly, but the thief also suffered a severe wound. Afterwards, the family heard the noise and got up to look. They saw a person covered in blood, crawling on the ground and moaning. Blood was flowing from his foot. They looked for A Long and found him floating in the water, which was turning red. They quickly pulled him out, but he was barely breathing and could not be saved. The next morning, they tied up the thief and sent him to the nearby security corps. They also chose a place to bury the dog and erected a monument next to the pond to commemorate him, writing in large characters: "On a certain day of a certain month in the Gengwu year, the loyal dog A Long died defending against thieves."

Memories of West Lake 180

— Tao Zaidong

West Lake's scenery is the most beautiful, but the embellishment of the landscape also relies on human effort. When I was magistrate of Hangzhou County, I once inscribed a chapter using Dongpo's words, "The Master of West Lake." During my tenure, I supervised the Lake Works Bureau, repairing famous scenic spots. The larger Yue Temple, Qian Shrine, and Yu Tomb were all completed during my tenure. Achieving things through people is the duty of an official, and there is nothing to praise. I just leave a few lines of writing for future generations to comment on. It's somewhat gratifying. What concerns me is the destruction of the fish-scale registers and the encroachment on public and private land. The beautiful West Lake is becoming fragmented. Forcible seizures and clever acquisitions cannot be restrained by law. Ancient sites are destroyed invisibly, and the lake itself is encroached upon over time. People do not hesitate to apply axes to ancient trees and sometimes dump waste into the drinking water. In a word, it's all for personal gain. When I judged lawsuits, I despised it in my heart. However, there are also people who are enthusiastic about public welfare. Wang Tiyu from Anhui is one of them. He built a garden at the foot of Nanping Mountain, and the construction was very beautiful. It contained many ancient artifacts, famous books, and paintings. He loved the *qin* and collected more than four hundred of them. He was a man of foresight. He once told me that he was willing to donate everything to Zhejiang Province for public ownership. This is truly rare. I quickly encouraged and supported him. He implemented it in 1926, formally submitting a petition to the county and then to the provincial government. The order was to commend him and instruct the county to consult with the gentry to discuss setting up a board of directors to manage the property. Before the matter was completed, I left office. It should be completed by now. This case originated in Wang's heart and was decided by Tao's hand. Not promoting it makes me feel like I have not fulfilled my duty. Recently, I saw in the newspaper that Wang's son had been kidnapped. The bandit case is a separate issue of social psychology. People often rejoice and rarely sympathize with wealthy people who have been captured by bandits. If this attitude is applied to Wang, it will frighten those who want to do good. This is saying something on behalf of West Lake. As for the construction of West Lake, it is wrong to think that it must rely on national funds. Read the West Lake Field Records. During the Ming Dynasty, Zhang, a eunuch, spent money, and the landscape was revitalized. Moreover, we are now in the Republic. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's six words, "of the people, by the people, for the people," are deeply rooted in people's hearts. How could there not be a second, even hundreds or thousands, of Wang Tiyus? The key is that good officials must guide and encourage them. Furthermore, there are too many ancestral halls and tombs in West Lake. Good mountains and waters are not used to plan entertainment methods for the living, but are occupied by the dead. This is a big mistake. Although it has been the custom for a long time, it should be corrected urgently. Moreover, since Su Xiao and Yue Fei's tombs have the phrase "heroes and heroines for thousands of years," ordinary people admire and imitate them, building tombs with fine workmanship and excellent stones, and inscribing tombstones. Seeing it makes me cringe, and thinking about it makes me angry. I think that a ban should be issued now, designating a scenic area along the lake and in the inner mountains for a certain number of *li*, prohibiting burials. Those who violate the law should be dismembered. This will prevent obstacles to future construction.

▲ Short News: Tuberculosis is a disease that is most difficult to cure. It has been repeatedly reported that people have expressed gratitude to the Yijin Herb of Peisheng Company on Zhonghua Road in Shanghai. Old cases of tuberculosis and coughing blood that have lasted for ten or twenty years have been cured by this herb and have not recurred. My old classmate, Mr. Wang, has suffered from this disease for fourteen years. Recently, I received a letter from him from Ningbo, saying that his illness suddenly worsened last autumn and he was on the verge of death. He also took this herb for forty days and recovered. Now his physique and spirit are getting stronger every day. It is heard that the Shanghai Siming Hospital has conducted practical research on this herb for two years and also believes that it is indeed a miraculous medicine for curing tuberculosis. I hereby issue a certificate to commend it. (Chen Ding)

Mr. Zhou has considerable friendships with many literary giants in Shanghai. Therefore, the works in this special issue are more than thirty in number, totaling more than one hundred pages, all of which are the best of the time. As for the exquisite printing, beautiful photos, and novel compilation, those are secondary matters. It is heard that it is scheduled to be published on April 1st and distributed by Huwei Trading Company on Renji Road. (Ziwei)

Now, there is a new translation of "Collection of Detective Novels by World Masters" published by Datong Bookstore. The collection lists the masterpieces of Sherlock Holmes, Arsène Lupin, Sondike, and others. All detective masterpieces from England, America, France, Russia, Austria, and other countries have been collected, which can be said to be a great compilation of detective novels.

The issue contains more than seventy photographs, all of which are masterpieces from the life of Mr. Dan Duyu. In addition, the inscriptions by Mr. Zheng Yimei are especially witty. Sleeping Pills Amidst Suicides 181

— Manyin

Every morning when we read the newspaper, the local social news that catches our eye the most is suicide news. This is not only true in prosperous Shanghai, but also in other places. There are various reasons for suicide, but most are economic, and a few are due to love. As for the method of suicide, taking medicine is the most common. In the past, people swallowed raw opium in the hope of ending their lives. Now, many people are taking an overdose of sleeping pills. This is especially true for young men and women in intellectual circles. They don't know where to buy opium, but there are pharmacies all over the city where they can buy sleeping pills. Also, the death from swallowing raw opium is quite tragic, while taking sleeping pills is like entering another world in a dream. It is now heard that the Executive Yuan of the National Government, in view of the increasing number of people committing suicide with sleeping pills, intends to devise methods to ban them. A citizen of Beiping, Men Jingyu, has also requested that the sale of sleeping pills be restricted as much as possible. The request has been forwarded by the Beiping Municipal Government. It is heard that the future methods of restriction will be: (1) Pharmacies will not be allowed to sell sleeping pills without a prescription signed by a responsible doctor. (2) When citizens purchase sleeping pills, their name, age, and detailed address should be investigated. (3) Each purchase should not exceed a single dose. It is said that the first article is a proper measure. As for the second article, those who intend to commit suicide may falsely report their name and address, making it impossible to investigate. Most of those who commit suicide in hotels now use fake names. As for the third article, it is a fundamental solution. However, they can still accumulate several doses and swallow them all at once. How can that be prevented? The Ministry of the Interior has ordered the Department of Health to properly draft measures to implement the ban. This is also a palliative measure. In short, if a person wants to die, everywhere becomes a path to death. In Shanghai, Zixia Paste is enough to destroy life, and the Huangpu River cannot be covered. Merely banning sleeping pills is not a fundamental solution.

Travelogue of India (XIV) 182

— Linghua

On the 2nd, Indian monk Shide Nazhao came to discuss matters of the Asian Cultural Association. He said that the university president could join. Shi accompanied me to visit the Victoria and Albert Museum, opposite the park. From the Buddhist Association, it costs six copper coins by tram. Upon entering, there are stone lions and ox statues displayed on both sides. The lion's head is damaged, and the ox has heads on all four sides. This is the Indian style, often seen. There is an inscription indicating that it was made by King Ashoka, around 240 B.C., a great protector of Buddhism. The museum is divided into two floors. There are many minerals that are difficult to identify. There are many small coral trees. There is a pair of large animal teeth, 84 English feet long. There is an Egyptian mummy, preserved with medicine and turned into a fossil, remaining intact to this day. It is from four thousand years ago. The patterns of the clothing still exist, but the face has become skeletal. Today, with the advancement of chemistry, this old method is no longer used. The most fascinating things are ancient steles, ancient bricks, ancient Buddha statues, and various Indian religious statues, which are very abundant. Those who want to study Indian history, culture, religion, art, and customs must study here. There are more than a hundred kinds of Indian writing, which we cannot recognize. There are also various kinds of Indian religious carvings, sculptures, and burnings. The materials are copper, iron, stone, brick, pottery, and soil of various colors. What is easy to see is that the statues are mostly unclothed. Even the Buddha statues are not covered in even an inch of silk. Also, the female statues have thin waists and very large breasts, similar to the style of Western women today. It can be seen that today's Western customs originated in India.

Items collected here come from various places. There are many from Nepal. There are many types of Tibetan Buddha statues. Those from Burma and various provinces of this country. There are many missing heads and feet. The small ones can be an inch in diameter, while the large ones are as tall as a person, either sitting or standing. If there are specialized Buddhists and those who can compare and study the traces of their changes with India, then there will definitely be great discoveries. I have seen various Buddha statues of Japanese Esoteric Buddhism. I also saw the Dunhuang Grottoes Thousand Buddha Paintings printed by the British at Yangon University, all in five colors, shining brightly. China cannot dream of it. When rituals are lost, seek them in the wild. Learn from the four barbarians. The quintessence of the nation also falls behind foreigners. This is a great shame.

The museum contains agricultural, cotton, silk, and porcelain items, but no machines. It can be seen that Indian machine science is not developed. There are many universities in various provinces of India, with thousands of students. The market is full of English writings by Indians in bookstores, far exceeding China. But they do not know how to learn machines, so they cannot compete with the British.

There is a Burmese throne, which is said to have been moved here after the destruction of the last kingdom. It is quite gorgeous.

The Victoria Queen statue in the west building facing east is made of marble and was completed in 1877. It was commemorated in the name of the Indian people. In the statue, the left hand holds a wreath, and the right hand holds a short baton, about a foot long. The goddess is graceful and elegant. It is the queen who annexed the entire India. I asked the Indians. The British map of India began with the East India Trading Company in the sixteenth century, gradually encroaching and annexing the entire India. It has been nearly a hundred years. The absorption of various provinces varies from early to late, some for two hundred years, some for one hundred and forty years, until today. Indians are beginning to awaken greatly and resist to the end.

The Guangbang agents are the most vigorous for current yarn and have a developing outlook, so the market sentiment is better. Large traders have high hopes and no intention of easing up. 300 bales of current yarn were traded in the morning, and there was no market in the afternoon. Grain: Price of Customer Sen Lower, Sales Moving 186

Ningbo, Guangdong, and Hoarders All Inquiring

Yesterday, the customer *sen* market remained weak. The Jiangxi agents, due to the weather getting warmer, could no longer hold on and were willing to reduce prices to sell. The customer agents had no way out for a long time and took advantage of this price weakness to conduct some trial transactions. If they could sell successfully, there would be progress in the future. Also, 600 bags of *mo* early goods were priced at 9.20 yuan to 9.00 yuan, bought by the Ningbo agent, Guangdong agent, and hoarders. The Guangdong agent also handled 608 bags of Jiangxi machine *yuan* by Zhongguan, priced at 11.50 yuan. After this batch is sold, if there are more sales in the future, the market price will definitely rebound.

Starch Market Gradually Declining 187

In the morning after the opening of the market for daily starch, prices for each month have dropped one after another, and the nearby and distant categories have returned to about 0.02. The reason for this is that despite the continuous price increases in the market, there have been no actual sales, and the goods that factories and merchants have ordered have not yet arrived. (Boat not arrived). Because there is more than enough remaining balance, they can take advantage of this high price to sell and set prices. The theory of the foreign wheat ban does not have to do with the current suspension of orders. The new wheat is growing very well, and inland gangs continue to sell. Therefore, the market price of each month has seen a gradual decline. Although there was a slight replenishment of short positions before the close of the market in the afternoon, the prices were still about 0.025 lower compared to the closing price of the previous day.

Wheat Market Plunges After Rising Sharply 188

After the opening of the wheat market yesterday, all months saw an improvement due to the previous day's increase. Subsequently, merchants who had ordered foreign wheat sold it off, and inland gangs continued to sell it off, and there was a renewed determination in thought of selling shorts, and it was followed by sales, and the market prices for all months fell sharply and uniformly. The new wheat standards for the months of June and below were because the scheduled arrival period for the previously ordered foreign wheat coincided with the time when the new wheat entered the market, and the short side was even more selling off. The market prices were even smaller than the recent ones. The closing prices were 0.05 less for July, 0.04 less for August and September, and 0.02 or 0.03 less for April and May.

Women's Life

The Life of Professional Women in New York 192

— Lin

(IV) This Freedom

After the rainbow, there is freedom. This is the cry of twentieth-century women. Historically speaking, female independence is a very new thing. How can it not be surprising? Although the exact date is hard to recall, it hasn't been long since women cast their first votes. Twenty years ago, you would never hear of a young woman going to New York alone to find a position and struggle with fate. Now, thousands of young women go to New York every year.

What is the meaning of this freedom? What does it encompass? It means making your own decisions, and there is no room for recriminations, no matter what the outcome. It means living alone, or with other women of the same generation, but not like a female dormitory supervisor in an old school. It means often supporting oneself. It means choosing to study what interests you, and if you enjoy watching plays, you can go out for a walk alone at midnight. In short, it is truly like the independence of a married woman without the heavy responsibilities.

Many parents are very unwilling to have their daughters live alone in New York City. Parents really don't understand that in today's world, there is an unwritten saying called "Youth Reigns." The old ways have changed. Young people today all want to try their wings and find their own way. Parents who oppose this argument stand on losing ground.

Professional women in New York who do not live with their families have complete freedom. First, their professions will never interfere with their social lives. In small cities, colleagues are very clear about each other's private actions. In New York City, because of the large area and population, professional women can disappear as soon as they leave the office. What she does is all her own business until she goes to work the next morning.

Living in New York City, neighbors mostly do not communicate with each other. Therefore, some people live in co-op apartments for several years without knowing the other residents. The shackles of social interaction are completely gone. Professional women do not need to worry about the surveillance of neighbors. She can think and do as she pleases. For truly powerful women, this is truly a glory. An individual's honest and self-confident behavior does not need to be interfered with by outdated traditions. Women who lack extremely valuable character and happiness are a little worse off. They cannot distinguish true value, and sometimes they are deceived by beauty and desire, and suffer pain. Parents raise their daughters and think about them, knowing under what circumstances they can find victory. (To be continued)

Page 23

Youth Corner

Sandalwood Beads 193

— Su Jun

Because I was suffering too much from neurasthenia, I came to live in West Lake on the advice of friends. Almost another week has passed. Unaccustomed to solitude and silence, I am hiding in a small house next to the cemetery of a revolutionary martyr on the shore of the lake. Loneliness occupies my surroundings. Except for seeing a doctor twice and taking a walk on Su Causeway in the evening, I live in such a large, quiet space. To be honest, my nerves are constantly suffering, because lonely shouting is a kind of suicide.

In the evening, I went to mail letters to friends and took a walk. On the road, I suddenly remembered Uncle Six's instructions to bring him a string of sandalwood beads. So I entered Yue Wang Temple. There were many stalls selling sandalwood beads and other items at the entrance of the temple, but I walked inside, under that big tree. I went to a stall selling sandalwood beads to pick and choose.

The seller of sandalwood beads was a girl. In her cheeks, her chest, the vague outline of her waist, and even the posture of her round hands and delicate feet, she was a mature girl, and she had considerable beauty, but it was simple and carried a slight seductive undertone. This was revealed in her smile and in the sound of her voice.

"These fragrances," she said, handing me many strings of beads, but her small, clever eyes were looking into space—she was not looking at any object.

"Oh," I smelled them, my nose close to her hand. She retracted her hand. I said, "Yes, but it's not as fragrant as your hand."

She was shocked by the customer's teasing. She turned her face and smiled. I also smiled.

I took a string and asked her,

"How much does it cost?"

"Six jiao."

"Six jiao?" I raised my eyebrows and stroked the sandalwood beads. Then I started to bargain with her. "It should be cheaper."

"What do you say?" She lowered the price for the customer.

"Four jiao, maybe," I said, "but I'm worried, I'm afraid these beads will become less fragrant."

"No way," she said, "You put them in your pocket, you put them on your arm, you gently stroke them, they won't be less fragrant."

"Yes, they will," I said stubbornly, "These beads, after I buy them, they will definitely be less fragrant."

"Why?"

"Yes," I said, sighing, "When they are with you, you will sprinkle the fragrant powder you put on your face on them, or they can be stained with the fragrance on your hands and the sweat mixed with fragrant powder dripping from your face at any time. However, they will be unfortunate because after I buy them..."

"Oh," she smiled, "You are so humorous."

"It's not a joke," I said, "I still won't buy them, right? If they really become less fragrant, then I will definitely abandon them. Oh, wouldn't that be too unfortunate?"

…" She laughed. She couldn't understand because I talked too much. Indeed, what I said later was not teasing, but truly a sense of sadness.

"I'll sell them to you for four jiao," she said, "They won't be less fragrant as long as you don't let them be exposed to wind and rain, and you play with them carefully. They will be fragrant for a long time."

"Oh," I said with a smile, "Just like your hands are tender for a long time, and your smile remains for a long time. The beads will also be fragrant for a long time."

"Yes," she said, "as long as you play with them carefully..."

She suddenly turned her head, silently stroking the sandalwood beads with her hands in place and space.

I left four jiao on the stall, on top of the sandalwood beads. I stroked a string of sandalwood beads and quietly walked away.

A funny sigh slipped out of my heart.

Renting a House and Women 194

— Zhan Bi

It has been several dozen days into the twentieth year of the Republic of China. Many schools in this city are busy with the start of school. My two younger sisters are also busy moving into the school.

The two of them live in the front building, and I live alone in the pavilion room. I got up this morning and went to the front building to wash my face. Younger Sister Ying and Younger Sister Zhen were discussing giving up the house. I said, "There is no point in discussing anything, once this front building is given up." Younger Sister Ying said with a smile,

"Do you understand the rules of Shanghai?"

"How can I not understand?"

"He is an old Shanghainese, of course he will understand,"

Younger Sister Zhen said with a sneer. Younger Sister Ying continued,

"Now it is the twelfth month of the lunar calendar. The landlord is a feudal-minded person. He wants to celebrate the lunar New Year. He will not allow us to give up the house in the two months surrounding the New Year, December and January. If you go to give up the house, I don't see how you can succeed. So I am discussing it with my sister."

"Oh, you can't give it up? How can you not give it up? Watch me, I'll go give it up. In the end, we men can give it up. As for you women, I'm afraid it won't be very successful."

Younger Sister Zhen just smiled. Younger Sister Ying said angrily,

"I'll see you go and give it up. If you can give it up, then I'll say you men have more insight. If you can't give it up, then when you come back late tonight, I will definitely not let you in and make you stand in that open-air dam all night to punish you for the sin of being a chatterbox."

"Okay, okay," I said with a sigh and a laugh as I walked downstairs to find the landlord.

There were originally many landlords. There were more than ten people in their family. However, the person in charge was an old lady, an old lady in her fifties. This old lady was very amiable and kind. A kind of approachable and admirable smile often appeared on her face. We have lived here for four months since we came to Shanghai this time. She has talked with our three sisters almost every day. She always asks about our daily life, food, clothing, and shelter, and she is very concerned. One day, Younger Sister Ying was wearing thinner clothes. She touched her body and pinched her shoulders, saying with great concern,

"Oh, sister, you quickly put on more clothes. The weather is very cold. If you get cold, it's not good. If you get sick, it's really worrying."

Another day, she saw that Younger Sister Zhen hadn't gotten out of bed. She sat on the edge of the bed and touched Younger Sister Zhen's head with her hand. She said anxiously,

"Oh, her forehead is burning badly. Mr. Zhan, quickly invite a doctor to feel her pulse. It's best to take medicine quickly."

"My brother is not at home. He went to Wusong this morning,"

Younger Sister Ying replied to her. She immediately left the edge of the bed, walking and saying,

"I'll help you invite a doctor. The doctor diagonally opposite Yadao Gate is a female doctor and is very good. I'll help you invite her."

She treats us with care just like a loving mother. Just now, my younger sisters said they were discussing the issue of giving up the house, probably because of the old lady's loving and amiable feelings that the discussion arose.

As soon as I walked into her room, she saw me.

"Mr. Zhan, you got up very early,"

"It's not early, it's nine o'clock. I really like to sleep late,"

"Early, very early. It's cold. There are many people in Shanghai who don't get up until twelve o'clock."

"Old lady, we want to give up the house. We're not living in the front building anymore."

"Oh, give up the house, good, good. Where are you moving to? Why only give up the front building?"

"My younger sisters are going to school. They will be moving into the school the day after tomorrow. I will still be living here."

"Go to school, that's good."

"I'm really sorry to you. We shouldn't be giving up the house in December of the lunar calendar."

"Oh, Mr. Zhan, please don't say that. Two girls are going to school. It doesn't matter if you give up the house in December of the lunar calendar. Anyway, we ourselves are short of houses to live in. You see, my grandson, he just came from the north. He doesn't have a house to put his bed in now. You see, he's sleeping on the table."
